ROOOOOBB VS COOOOKKKINNNG
If you ever decide to try this again, my suggestion is to make donut BOWLS (drape dough over a small ceramic bowl to cook) and then put the cooked donut bowls in a bigger bowl.  A) easier to safely eat more than one fried scoop at a time and B) a LOT neater!    I think the cinnamon rolls idea would work if they were only one layer and more carefully coiled around a bowl.  And even if the bowl wasn't perfect, eating it inside another bowl would make it function, even if there were gaps.  You should do this again, with croissants and cinnamon rolls to see which works better as bowls and do a re-test! :D

for future reference: for burns, mix some baking soda with water until it's a pasty texture, put it on a burn, as soon as possible after you are burnt, keep it there until it comes off on its own.  it reduces the pain and swelling, and there's less of a chance to get a blister.  You're welcome.

Just a tip from a person that always makes bread and other stuff with yeast: set the milk at around 38ÂºC (to check for temperature, you can touch it with the inside of your wrist. It should feel a bit warm, but not feel like it is burning). Then leave it for 10 minutes.  Also, avoid letting salt touch the yeast directly. It will kill the yeast and reduce its effectiveness if you do.  Either way, more of this! :D

The original one is actually cylinder shaped and called chimneycake(kÃ¼rtÅ‘skalÃ¡cs) in hungarian. The traditional baking is on a wooden stick above fire. And you first have to cure the wood with oil, then roll the dough just like you guys did to it, then bake the dough without sugar! halfway put some more oil to the dough and then put it to sugar, so it will caramellize, and at the end they put it in sugar again. That caramel layer makes it yellow, not the eggwash. There's no eggwash, although I have no idea how they make the cone shapes to the trend maybe you should have tried the oil, and baking it halfway so the sugar wouldn't crack off. Ok I was pretty interested in this one, cause TrdelnÃ­k is pretty much a thing here (imma from Czech republic. But the origin of the TrdelnÃ­k is from Skalica in Slovakia and actually... it's so different from the normal selling shit. The one from Skalica like... melts on your tongue and is so fluffy and covered in powdered suger. The best fucking thing you can get. And it's kinda secret recipe or something like that because this is the only brand of Trdelnik that tastes this way.). So yeah suprise me.  -Also yeast is good to be kept in warm place. When we do this in winter mom always puts it on heater so it has nice and cozy place when it can do its thing.  -And the dough... its better not to cover it with plastic. Use cloth insted. So it can breath. Because yeast is a living organism. It needs air so it could double in size.  -TrdelnÃ­k is made a kinda special way. On one sided grill or how you call that shit. Its just roling all the time and the heat is just on one side and it rolls all the time until its done. Mayb thats one of the reason why it didnt work like you imagined.

you have to activate the gluten in the flour so when the yeast dies the air doesn't gets out and the bread gets fluffy and light. so after you formed the dough you want to throw it on the counter for at least 10-20 min. best way to release stress and work your arm muscles. do it as hard as you can. then leave it rest and it will "grow" (but it's just the yeast breathing and the air getting trapped by the gluten). Here's a random, funny, true story. Many years ago, on a hot summer day, my Aunt was in her car, parked somewhere in an area where gunshots are unfortunately not uncommon (South Boston). All of a sudden she heard a pop and felt something hit the back of her head. Thinking she'd just heard a gunshot and fearing she'd been shot, she reached up and felt what she thought was her brains coming out of her head. So, she sat there waiting to inevitably die (these were before the days of cell phones). After a few moments of not dying she began to investigate the situation and found a Grands Biscuit container in her backseat that had exploded due to the heat in the car.
